Player_Black (to Proxy):

**Step 1: Analyze the current board state.**  
Black has a knight on e4, which is centrally positioned. White’s king is on e1 with limited escape squares, and the rook on h1 is undefended. White’s queen is off the board, severely weakening their position.

**Step 2: Identify critical weaknesses and tactics.**  
The knight on e4 can deliver a **fork** by moving to **f2**, attacking both the king and the rook. White’s king has no defenders nearby, and the rook on h1 is vulnerable.

**Step 3: Execute the strongest tactical move.**  
`make_move e4f2`  
This forces White’s king to move (e.g., Ke2, Kd1, or Kf1), after which Black can capture the undefended rook on h1 with the knight, gaining material and initiative.

Player_Black (to Proxy):

The best move in this position is **d4e2**, capturing the white pawn on e2 and delivering a check to the white king. This move immediately wins material and disrupts White's position. Here's the breakdown:

1. **Forcing the King to Move**: After d4e2+, White’s king on e1 is in check and must move to d1 or f1. This forces White into a passive position.
2. **Follow-Up Material Gain**:  
   - If the king moves to **d1**, Black’s knight can capture the bishop on c1 (e2xc1), winning a minor piece.  
   - If the king moves to **f1**, Black’s knight can capture the knight on g1 (e2xg1), trading knights but still netting a pawn.  
3. **Initiative and Pressure**: The knight becomes a central attacking piece, creating further threats in White’s camp.

This tactical shot maximizes Black’s advantage by combining material gain with positional pressure.

Player_Black (to Proxy):

make_move d4d1

**Step-by-Step Explanation:**

1. **Check Opportunity:** The rook on d4 can move to d1, delivering a check to the White king on g1. This forces the king to move off the first rank.
2. **Forced King Movement:** After 1...Rd1+, the White king must move to g2, h2, or f2. Let's assume Kh2 (other squares lead to similar outcomes).
3. **Follow-up Check:** The bishop on b3 moves to e2 (2...Be2+), checking the king again. The king is forced to h3 (since g3 is blocked by a White pawn).
4. **Checkmate:** The rook on d1 moves to h1 (3...Rh1#), delivering checkmate as the king has no escape squares (h4 and g4 are controlled by the rook and bishop, respectively).

This sequence results in a forced checkmate in three moves.

Player_Black (to Proxy):

The move **f6g5** is illegal because knights move in an L-shape (2 squares in one direction, then 1 square perpendicular). From **f6**, valid moves for the black knight are **d5**, **h5**, **e4**, or **g4**. Here's the correction:

**make_move f6g4**

This moves the knight from f6 to g4, following the correct L-shaped path (2 squares down, 1 square right).

The best move here is to check the white king with the rook, forcing it into a mating net. 

**Step-by-Step Explanation:**
1. **Rook Check**: Move the rook from e7 to f7 (`e7f7`), delivering a check to the white king on f5.
2. **Force King Movement**: The white king must move to g5, the only safe square.
3. **Pawn Push**: Advance the h7 pawn to h6 (`h7h6`), preparing the square for the rook.
4. **Rook Check Again**: Move the rook from f7 to g7 (`f7g7`), forcing the king to h5.
5. **Checkmate**: Finally, move the rook to h7 (`g7h7`), delivering checkmate as the king has no escape squares.

This sequence leads to a forced checkmate in four moves.

**Move:**  
`make_move e7f7`
